Radio Broadcast

"The Shanghai Children's Broadcasting Competition jointly organized by the Shanghai Radio Station (XOHC) of the Ministry of Communications and the China National Goods Company" is scheduled to be held from today to the 7th. Many children in the city have enthusiastically signed up to participate. As of yesterday, more than 400 people had passed the preliminary rounds and achieved excellent results. Mayor Wu and Education Director Pan have each donated a large silver shield to reward the first place winners in groups A and B. In addition to valuable prizes for the top ten, all those who pass the preliminary rounds and participate in the competition will also receive awards. All the prizes are donated by various national goods factories. It is also heard that the station has hired Director Pan, Jiang Jianbai, Yao Zhenyu, Ding Shoutang, and Lu Hailan to serve as judges.

British Officials and Citizens in Shanghai Prepare to Celebrate King's Accession Anniversary, Hosting Chinese and Foreign Officials and Reviewing Troops 119

The British Consulate General in Shanghai and British merchants in Shanghai are preparing a grand celebration for the 25th anniversary of the accession of King George next month on the 6th, which is approaching. A decorated archway has been erected in front of the British Consulate on the Bund. At that time, celebrations will be held to host Chinese and foreign officials in Shanghai, and the stationed naval and army troops in Shanghai will be reviewed.

Tang Xifen Discusses Past London Art Exhibitions 120

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Pre-exhibition of the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art, which has been in preparation for a long time, has been properly arranged and is scheduled to open on the 8th. A Central News Agency reporter visited Mr. Tang Xifen, the secretary of the exhibition, yesterday to inquire about everything. He kindly provided detailed information about each country's art exhibition held in London, which can be used for our reference and learning, as well as the details of the pre-exhibition. The details are recorded below.

Seven Times

According to him, the Burlington House of the Royal Academy of Arts in England has successively held international art exhibitions for Finland, the Netherlands, Italy, Persia, France, and Britain in recent years. The Chinese art exhibition, which will be held in November of this year, will be the seventh.

Purpose of Holding

The reason why countries do not hesitate to hold large-scale international art exhibitions in England is mainly to reflect the spiritual sustenance of various ethnic groups over the years and to express the achievements of their creative abilities, so that visitors can understand the corresponding status of various ethnic groups, thereby promoting international friendship and obtaining huge political, economic, and even commercial benefits. Its value has already been established and should not be doubted in the slightest.

Past Experiences

The holding of international art exhibitions in England began with Finland in 1927, and the exhibition lasted about eight weeks. The second was the Netherlands in 1929, with a similar duration as Finland. Then there were Italy (1930), Persia (1931), France (1932), and Britain (1934). The exhibitions lasted either ten weeks or nine weeks, but the difference was not significant.

Each Organization

Generally, the heads of state of the two countries serve as supervisors, the administrative leaders of the two countries serve as honorary presidents, and important political figures and social celebrities from the two countries serve as honorary committee members. In addition, there is a board of directors composed of the initiators and the main institutions providing exhibits from each country and the Royal Academy of Arts in England to execute and direct everything. Under the board of directors, there are committees for display, finance, and selection to handle various matters. At the same time, in order to widely collect exhibits, solicitation committees are established separately in various countries.

Source of Funds

Most of the funds come from ticket sales. The ticket price is five shillings (about seven yuan in Chinese currency) on Fridays, and one shilling and six pence (about two and a half yuan in Chinese currency) on other days. Each art exhibition has a surplus after deducting all expenses. When Italy held the international art exhibition, Prime Minister Mussolini had pre-allocated 20,000 pounds, but in the end, not a penny was used, and a surplus of 37,000 pounds was obtained.

Exhibiting Institutions

Generally, the treasures collected by museums run by the countries and provinces are the main exhibits, and the collections of various groups and individuals are solicited to supplement them. For example, the international art exhibition held by Persia collected exhibits from more than 200 museums, libraries, and more than 30 countries. In addition, there were more than 300 pieces of private exhibits.

Number of Exhibits

It is difficult for each country to have the same number of exhibits. Generally speaking, it is between 1,000 and 2,000 pieces.

Types of Exhibits

The types of exhibits in each country's art exhibition are extremely diverse, and they are not entirely the same in each country. In addition to books, bronzes, porcelains, jade articles, etc., there are also pottery, goldware, silverware, glassware, textiles, wood carvings, lace, furniture, sculptures, etc.

Era of Exhibits

The exhibits from France and Italy range from 1200 to 1900. Other countries are roughly the same. However, Persia is an ancient civilization, so there are many prehistoric exhibits.

Other Activities

In addition to the exhibition itself, each country's art exhibition also has other subsidiary activities to promote publicity. There are usually three ways: first, experts give lectures on the culture and art of each country; second, famous music from each country is played. Both of the above two require separate admission tickets. Third, commemorative albums and exhibit catalogs are sold, and famous book plates of collotype and copper prints are sold. The above sections are the general situation of the international art exhibitions held by various countries in England. As for the purpose and organization of our country's exhibition, they are roughly the same.

Mu Li Tusi's Petition Representatives Pass Through Shanghai, Scheduled to Go to Beijing This Morning to Petition 121

The Mu Li Nine Tribes Tusi, located at the intersection of Sichuan, Kang, and Yunnan provinces, and under the jurisdiction of Yanyuan County in Sichuan, due to being unable to bear Liu Wenhui's brutality, specifically sent representatives Xi Luo Jixiang, along with religious representative Yue Wu Yeda, and public representative Song Nuo Jize, three people, to Beijing to petition. When they left Sichuan, Liu's troops conducted extremely strict inspections, and they suffered many hardships along the way. They arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and are staying at the Ping An Hotel in the French Concession. Due to the fatigue of the journey, Mr. Yue Wu Yeda is feeling slightly unwell and is temporarily resting at the hotel. Yesterday, Mr. Xie Jiewu accompanied Xi Luo Jixiang and Song Nuo Jize to the hotel, and discussed with reporters Liu's oppression of the Tusi. Mr. Xi Luo Jixiang does not understand Chinese, and although Mr. Song Nuo Jize can speak Chinese, he is not very fluent, so Mr. Xie translated on their behalf. The two gentlemen were dressed entirely in Han Chinese clothing, and were polite and courteous. They said that they would go to Beijing this morning to petition the authorities. During the conversation, they produced their mimeographed draft telegram and asked for it to be announced on their behalf. Before leaving, they performed a religious ceremony, clasped their hands together, and bowed. The original text is recorded as follows: To all national agencies, legal entities, newspapers, and all fathers, brothers, sisters, and aunts across the country for your information. The Mu Li Nine Tribes Tusi, located in Yanyuan County, southern Sichuan, at the intersection of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Kang provinces, is the gateway to the three provinces. Since submitting to the Qing Dynasty during the Kangxi period, for more than three hundred years, they have lived in peace. Since the founding of the Republic of China, Sichuan has been plagued by constant turmoil. The authorities have abused the border people, treating them as uncivilized outsiders. No one has cared about any administrative measures. As a result, banditry has become increasingly rampant, and the people are living in misery. Our Mu Li Nine Tribes Tusi, witnessing the difficulties of the times, are deeply concerned. Considering the importance of border defense, they have strived to find ways to defend themselves. For the past twenty years, they have finally relied on the collective efforts of the people to avoid collapse. After Liu Wenhui's defeat and retreat to Ya'an in the twenty-first year, more than ten thousand of his troops were scattered throughout southern Sichuan, and Mu Li Nine Tribes was also occupied. Arbitrary donations and miscellaneous taxes were imposed repeatedly, and the people have long groaned under oppression, living a life worse than death. Recently, Liu has even rashly listened to rumors and coveted the wealth of Mu Li, ordering the Tusi to hand over gold mines and sending troops to mine them. Since the Donglao Mountain mine was empty and the work yielded little results, he not only did not repent, but instead vented his anger on the Mu Li Tusi, forcing them to point out other gold-producing locations and demanding compensation for losses of 200,000 taels of silver. In the future, the monthly salaries and food expenses of the factory troops should be borne by the Tusi, otherwise he would launch a large-scale punitive expedition to interrogate them. This kind of absurd order was relayed by Shen Hong, the magistrate of Yanyuan County. After hearing the order, the Tusi were terrified and at a loss. They immediately sent leaders to Yanyuan, requesting Magistrate Shen to intercede on their behalf. Magistrate Shen replied in a letter, stating that the original order of 200,000 taels was equivalent to 280,000 yuan in foreign currency, but 130,000 yuan could be reduced, and they still had to pay 150,000 yuan quickly. The order was like a mountain, and they must not provoke his anger, etc. They then sent leaders several times to beg for leniency, but were not granted permission. Military force was used to oppress them, and the situation was tense. It was as if they would live if they had money, and die if they did not. The extent of their cruelty to the people was extreme. The general public was filled with resentment and repeatedly thought of taking the risk of fleeing to avoid this calamity. However, the Tusi had received the grace of the state for generations and could not bear to abandon their homeland lightly and be ridiculed by foreigners. Therefore, they tried to persuade the public to endure for a while and simultaneously appealed to the central government to await legal action. However, Liu Wenhui, with the heart of a beast, had long disregarded the country. Hearing that the Tusi had submitted a petition to the central government, he was enraged and sent his henchman Li Zhangfu to lure Xiang Ci Chengzha, the Mu Li Yiwei Si, who was directly appointed by the central government, and assassinate him at a meeting place. He then kidnapped the current Mu Li Tusi Zha Ba Songdian and imprisoned him in Yanyuan County as a hostage. Not only did he not reduce any of the previous debts, but he also forced them to hand over 500 large rifles, 40 small rifles, and 60,000 rounds of ammunition, and threatened to execute the Mu Li Tusi if they did not comply. The Tusi, witnessing this brutality, felt even more grief, and the people of the Nine Tribes were even more in imminent danger. Therefore, they convened a general assembly of the Nine Tribes' customs and people to discuss solutions. After deliberation, three matters were decided, which are now tearfully reported to the officials of our government and compatriots across the country: (1) Send representatives to Beijing to petition, demanding that the central government punish Liu Wenhui, who arbitrarily killed central government officials, in order to redress the grievances of Xiang Ci Chengzha and comfort the hopes of the monks and people of the Nine Tribes. (2) Request the central government to order Liu Wenhui to immediately release Zha Ba Songdian and ensure his safety, and return him to Mu Li to govern. All of Liu's troops should withdraw from Mu Li without exception and not use mining as an excuse to trample on the borderlands. (3) The people of the Nine Tribes vow to be irreconcilable with Liu Wenhui. Request the central government to clearly delineate the Mu Li Nine Tribes Tusi territory under the jurisdiction of Yunnan Province and permanently sever its relationship with Sichuan. As the ancients said, "Cherish us, we will follow; abuse us, we will hate." Liu Wenhui's treatment of Mu Li can truly be described as irreconcilable. Our border people can hardly bear to serve him with a smile and be ridiculed by the world. The above three points are the fundamental plan, and we hope that the officials of our government and compatriots across the country will uphold their spirit of supporting the weak, advocate justice, speak out righteously, and rescue us so that we can escape from fire and water and ascend to a comfortable seat. This will not only be the fortune of the Nine Tribes but also admired by all sides, for upholding laws and protecting the territory lies herein. The people of Mu Li Nine Tribes have reached the extreme point of anger. If the situation is not reported, and they take the risk of causing chaos, then the region will be troubled from now on, and the nation's border defenses will be lost.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submits Urgent Request to Ministry of Finance to Quickly Allocate Funds to Aid Industry and Commerce, Bank of China Increases Official Shares, Submits Receipt to Ministry, Bank of Communications Schedules Regular Shareholders' Meeting 122

After receiving instructions from the Ministry of Finance and accepting the resolutions of the 18th Shareholders' Meeting, the Board of Directors of the Bank of China decided to return two of the five notes of the 25 million yuan financial public bonds of the Republic of China given by the Ministry on the 28th of last month, totaling 10 million yuan, and simultaneously filled out a receipt for 15 million yuan in official shares. As for Article 2 of the regulations, the revised total amount of share capital is 50 million yuan, divided into 500,000 shares, each share being 100 silver yuan, with 300,000 official shares and 200,000 commercial shares. Now, it is decided to revise it again to 40 million yuan, divided into 400,000 shares, with 200,000 official shares and 200,000 commercial shares, to be submitted by the Ministry of Finance to the National Government for promulgation.

Bank of Communications to Hold Shareholders' Meeting

The total amount of share capital of the Bank of Communications is 10 million yuan, with 8 million yuan in commercial shares and 2 million yuan in official shares. After the Ministry of Finance allocated 10 million yuan in financial public bonds of the Republic of China as official shares, the regulations have also been revised, and the number of directors and managing directors has been increased. The Bank of Communications has scheduled to hold this shareholders' meeting at 1:00 PM on April 20 at the Bank Association on Hong Kong Road. In addition to the business report, the increase of shares will also be discussed. The term of office of the twelve commercial share directors has not expired, so they will remain the same. However, the term of office of the four commercial share supervisors has expired and should be re-elected immediately. As for the increase in official share directors and supervisors, it will be appointed by the Ministry of Finance.

China Handles Closing Procedures After Suspension of U.S. Cotton and Wheat Loan, Purchased Cotton Totals More Than 40 Million Yuan 131

According to Huadong News Agency, yesterday morning, the Huadong News Agency reporter specifically inquired with relevant parties and learned that China's negotiations with the United States for the cotton and wheat loan have been suspended. The reason for the loan was that in 1933, China's cotton and wheat production had sharply decreased, so former Finance Minister Song Ziwen negotiated a U.S. cotton and wheat loan of 50 million U.S. dollars with the U.S. side. After this loan was established, China happened to establish the Cotton Industry Control Association, which greatly increased the domestic production of cotton and wheat, and the demand suddenly decreased. In addition, Japanese yarn factories in China have always purchased cotton from China for their use. When the U.S. cotton loan was established, the Japanese side expressed opposition, and the Japanese yarn factories' purchase of cotton from China was immediately suspended. As a result, China's sales market for U.S. cotton decreased, so it implemented the closure of the purchase of U.S. cotton. Now China has already handled the closing of the purchase of cotton. According to China's conclusion of the U.S. cotton and wheat contract with the United States in 1933, the U.S. cotton and wheat loaned amounted to 17,105,385 yuan, equivalent to more than 40 million Chinese yuan.

Land Registration Can Use Agency System 132

Lawyer Hu Fenglian, a member of the Shanghai Bar Association, accepted the entrustment of his client and made a suggestion, requesting the Executive Supervisory Committee of the association to forward a letter to the Shanghai Land Bureau, requesting changes to the transfer registration of land sales and purchases, as well as mortgage registration, etc., to facilitate the process. After the meeting decided to forward the letter to the Municipal Land Bureau, a reply letter was received from Jin Liren, the director of the Land Bureau yesterday, stating that the matter of requesting changes to the measures should be handled in accordance with Article 68 of the Land Law. Upon investigation, the reply letter stated, "Please change the measures for the transfer registration of land sales and purchases and mortgage registration, etc." Upon investigation, the transfer registration measures and real estate mortgage registration rules approved by the city for implementation do not have (agent) regulations. However, Article 68 of the Land Law states that "when registration is applied for by an agent, a letter of authorization should be attached." In the future, when there are agency cases, they can be handled in this way. A corresponding reply is sent for your reference. Respectfully, Jin Liren, Director of the Shanghai Land Bureau.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Public Works Bureau Requesting Prompt Dredging of Zoumatang City River 133

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter, on the 2nd of this month, according to a letter from the Wang Renzhong Baobo of the Gongwan Branch Office of our Chamber, the dredging project of the Zoumatang City River in this district has exceeded the deadline by two months and the dam has not yet been opened, causing difficulties in the transportation of goods, and the accumulated water is stagnant, emitting odors, which is also detrimental to hygiene. Moreover, the spring plowing season is approaching, and irrigation is urgently needed, so opening the dam as soon as possible cannot be delayed. It is rumored that this is because the bridge is being rebuilt and the project has not yet been completed, so there is a saying that the dam will not be opened for a while. If this is true, it is suggested to partially enclose the dam in the area where the bridge reconstruction project is located, and the east and west ends can be opened first to allow ships to pass separately to alleviate the urgency, even if it cannot be passed through in one go, it will also be very convenient, for which a special document is prepared, hoping that the Municipal Public Works Bureau will review and transfer it to open the dam immediately, and transportation and hygiene will all benefit from it, and the farmers will also deeply appreciate it, etc., to the Chamber. Based on this, upon investigation, the Public Works Bureau replied in a letter on October 5, 1933, stating that workers had been dispatched to start work on the 16th of last month. Now, more than two years have passed, and the river project has not yet been completed, causing the dam to be blocked, which is not only causing great difficulties in commercial transportation, but also the weather is getting hotter and the sewage is stagnant, which is detrimental to public health, which is also not insignificant. The branch office advocates to measure the garden dam in the area where the bridge is being rebuilt, and the east and west ends can be opened first, which is to seek convenient transportation in a helpless situation. A corresponding letter is sent to inform you of the situation, hoping that your bureau will review and transfer it to be handled immediately, and also order the river works department to completely dredge and open the dam on a specific day to benefit farmers and merchants, and be deeply grateful."

Rice Riot in Qingpu County 134

The day before yesterday, a rice boat from Changshu, carrying 202 shi and 5 dou of white rice, arrived in Shanghai, traveling to Sigangkou, Shuangmiao area near Huangdu in the east. More than ten shi of white rice were robbed by the villagers there using small boats. The Shanghai North Rice Transporters' Association was asked to find out the details, and the association submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau, which was forwarded to the Municipal Government, requesting the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the competent authorities of Qingpu County to strictly investigate and protect the safety. The original submission is recorded as follows: "Submitting a report on the looting of rice by rioters in Qingpu territory, please immediately transfer it to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order an investigation to maintain rice transportation. According to the report of rice merchant Gu Sanbao, a member of the affiliated association, his boat loaded with 202 shi and 5 dou of white rice from Changshu set sail on March 28th. At 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 29th, when it arrived at Six Lane, the Shuangmiao area near Huangdu in the east, which is under the jurisdiction of Qingpu County, it suddenly encountered a small boat from the area, with eight strong men with local accents. They used the　 to drag the rice boat and ordered it to stop. They were immediately　 crowded onto the boat and robbed more than ten shi of white rice by force. At that time, there were as many as seventy or eighty spectators on both sides of the river, but they were not afraid at all, and after plundering, they leisurely sailed away. Afterwards, they immediately looked for　 the township head, and　 reported to the Huangdu District Office. The　 patrol chief came to the boat to investigate the case, and specially entrusted　 to investigate and deal with it. At the same time,　 according to various guests, the villagers there　 were called fierce, and if they were not severely punished,　 all the rice boats would not dare to go to Shanghai, etc., came forward. The act of gang robbery is indeed　 lawless. Various　 rice merchants, because they heard that the people's food security are all hindered　, should report the situation to your bureau and forward it to the Municipal Government, requesting the Jiangsu Provincial Government to order the competent authorities of Qingpu County to strictly investigate in order to protect safety and maintain rice transportation, and wait for orders. Presented by Wu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Shanghai Hub North Rice Transport Yongshang Lianyi Association."

Bean and Rice Traders Request Protection for Rice Shipments 135

The Bean and Rice Industry Association of this city, due to the Wusong River dredging and damming by the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission, which has caused inland rice boats heading to Shanghai to detour via Qingpu and Songjiang, encountering robberies, has specially submitted a petition by the association's chairman, Gu Xinyi, to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, earnestly requesting that the police be instructed to conduct strict patrols to protect the rice shipments. The original text is as follows:

We have recently learned that the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission is dredging the Yuji Mound section of the Wusong River, and work was completed on the first of April, damming the river. Merchants and shippers from inland areas selling rice in Shanghai are mostly detouring through Qingpu and Songjiang counties, then via the outer Huangpu River to reach Shanghai. At 2:00 AM on the 31st of last month, a boatman named Gu Sanbao, shipping rice from Changshu to Shanghai, detoured through Shuangmiao, which is under the jurisdiction of Qingpu County, and was suddenly robbed by local villagers who gathered in a mob, resulting in a loss of over 30 piculs of white rice. As word of this spreads, rice merchants and boatmen are feeling uneasy. Dredging the Wusong River is not something that can be accomplished overnight. However, during the damming period, customers are refraining from shipping due to the perceived danger of the route, which will inevitably affect the supply to the Shanghai market. Therefore, we are submitting this document to your esteemed office, requesting that you promptly notify the governments of Qingpu and Songjiang counties, instructing their respective water police to conduct strict patrols along the detour routes used by rice boats, to protect the rice shipments and ensure safe transport. We would be immensely grateful.

The wedding participants, officiant, witnesses, all city hall staff, and spectators inside and outside the hall numbered over ten thousand. Amidst the lively atmosphere, there was also a solemn air. The ceremony lasted one hour and fifteen minutes. A Central News Agency reporter has provided the following details:

A Glimpse of the Wedding Hall

The Party and national flags fluttered in front of the City Hall gate. The Party emblem and Party and national flags were fastened on the second-floor railings, creating a brand-new atmosphere. Flowers were arranged along the steps. In the center of the hall, a space was left, covered with a large red carpet leading directly to the stage. Numbers were placed side by side, and colored ribbons were arranged on both sides to create a standing area for the newlyweds awaiting the ceremony. Next to it was the officiant's seat. A pair of large candlesticks, each two feet tall, was placed in front of the stage, engraved with "May the offspring be numerous" and "Dragon and Phoenix bring prosperity." The stage was also fully covered with a red carpet. Flowers were displayed by the staircase. A portrait of Sun Yat-sen was placed on a table in front, with three pairs of red-covered chairs placed to the left and right. Two side tables were placed at the edge of the stage, holding certificates and souvenirs. Chairs were arranged on all four sides of the stage for the audience.

Enthusiastic Spectators

The brides and grooms, accompanied by their parents, arrived one after another, first going to the dining hall on the ground floor of the City Hall to sit down according to their assigned numbers and get ready. Guests from all walks of life gathered around the City Hall, in great numbers. The Public Security Bureau dispatched police to maintain order strictly. Those with tickets scrambled to get in, creating an unprecedented lively scene. All city hall staff members worked diligently in the hall to take care of everyone, especially Mayor Wu, who directed the arrangements, adding to the excitement. Celebrities such as Du Yuesheng and Wang Xiaoxu also attended the ceremony with their families.

Gracious Reception

The officiant was Mayor Wu Tiecheng, and the witness was Wu Xingya, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau. The master of ceremonies was Wang Xianqing. Sun Binghui, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, led the grooms, and Ms. Chen Guowei led the brides. Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Cai Jinjun, Director of the Public Security Bureau, Li Dachao, Section Chief of the Municipal Government, and Secretaries Zhang Tingrong and Tang Shixuan, and Wu Huanru, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, all wore blue robes and black mandarin jackets and provided guidance and reception on the spot. Because it was the first group wedding, all the arrangements took a lot of time, especially the brides getting ready, who arrived late, so the ceremony did not begin until 3:30 PM.

Newlyweds Enter

The Social Affairs Bureau sent four male and female staff members, holding gauze lanterns, to guide the brides and grooms separately from the rest area. When they entered the hall from the main staircase of the City Hall, the City Music Corps played music outside the hall. After entering, Ms. Zhang Tingrong's daughter, Lianqing, and four students from the National Conservatory of Music played the piano and violin, and the hall, which was initially noisy, suddenly became quiet, adding to the solemnity and grandeur of the wedding. The brides wore white dresses and veils, with badges and corsages on their chests, and held bouquets of flowers tied with pink ribbons. The grooms wore blue robes and black mandarin jackets, and each couple looked full of vitality.

Conducting the Ceremony

The wedding ceremony began, and to save time, it was changed to have two couples perform the ceremony at the same time. The master of ceremonies announced the names of both parties. The groom was led by Sun Binghui, and the bride was led by Chen Guowei. They ascended the stage from the side staircase, stood in front of Sun Yat-sen's portrait, and the master of ceremonies called out to pay the highest respect to the portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the Party and national flags, bowing three times. The bride and groom stood facing each other and bowed twice, returned to their positions, and bowed once to the officiant. Mayor Wu, who was standing to the left, presented the certificate to the groom, and Director Wu, who was on the right, presented the commemorative badge to the bride. They bowed once to thank the officiant, and the couple retreated hand in hand, standing in the designated position.

Reading the Testimony

After the ceremony, Mayor Wu read the testimony: "On the third day of April in the 24th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai Municipal Government held the first New Life Group Wedding Ceremony. Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Wu Xingya, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, are the witnesses." He officially announced that so-and-so (list of 57 couples) and other participants were legally married. Then he read the instructions (see yesterday's newspaper, details omitted here). The ceremony ended at 4:15 PM, and Ms. Zhang Lianqing played the piano as the brides and grooms exited the hall. Finally, at the open space, Wang Kai Photo Studio took a group photo.

Rivaling Film Shoots

The ceremony ended as dusk fell, but the crowd gathered in the square in front of the City Hall remained packed. The City Public Security Bureau Band played music again. The doors of the hall were wide open. The 57 pairs of brides and grooms followed the male and female staff of the City Hall, who carried bright horn lanterns and palace lanterns, and filed out in formation. As they slowly walked up the stone steps, the blue robes and black mandarin jackets contrasted with the white wedding dresses. From a distance, it looked like a floral pattern with oriental flavor, which can be called a spectacle. The Film Division of the Central Propaganda Department, as well as Paramount, MGM, Fox, and other film companies from the United States, sent photographers to the scene to compete in shooting newsreels. They will each send the films to major cities around the world using the fastest means of transmission. In one month, this world-rare group wedding ceremony will be seen by people in various countries. The brides and grooms stood in a semi-circular formation in front of the City Hall's noble steps for half an hour, allowing news reporters and photographers to take pictures. The Mayor and the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau also stood smiling in the center of this rosy formation. They dispersed around 6:00 PM.

Feasting with Relatives and Friends

Statistics show that the wedding ceremony lasted a total of one hour and fifteen minutes, which can be said to be extremely simple, but the solemn scene was unmatched by traditional weddings. Mayor Wu and Director Wu originally planned to provide refreshments for the newlyweds but changed the funds for this item to be used for commemorative gifts to pursue permanence and save time, so it was cancelled. For a time, the vehicles on the central district and Jiangwan Road were connected, and the crowds were packed, creating a joyful situation that had never been seen before. It is said that the newlyweds all feasted with relatives and friends last night to celebrate.

World Cruise: German Liner Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; After Sightseeing, Passengers Board Ship Tonight for Northbound Journey 141

According to the New Voice News Agency, the German Hapag-Lloyd's world cruise liner, the "Lissauer," carrying 297 tourists and over 100 crew members, departed from New York on January 12 for a world cruise. After more than two months, it arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning around 2:00 AM. The Hapag-Lloyd branch office on the Bund specially sent a small launch in advance to meet and guide the ship outside Wusongkou, as the liner was visiting Shanghai for the first time and was not very familiar with the Huangpu River route. When it docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf in Hongkou, the passengers were still asleep, so they did not disembark at that time. They all went ashore after breakfast around 8:00 AM.

Touring the Entirety of Shanghai

The 200-plus tourists disembarked at 8:30 AM after breakfast. The company had pre-rented over 200 cars to carry the tourists from the pier to the French Concession and Longhua. Then, via the Fawangdu Garden in West Shanghai, Nanjing Road, and Henan Road, they went to Zhabei Jiangwan to inspect the January 28th Battle Zone. Finally, they went via North Sichuan Road to the Astor House Hotel on the Waibaidu Bridge to rest and have lunch. In the afternoon, around 2:00 PM, the tourists re-embarked, taking over 300 rickshaws to visit the Nanshi and City God Temple, visiting bird markets, teahouses, etc., as these social situations were all unseen by these tourists. They finished their tour around 6:00 PM and had dinner on the ship. Around 8:00 PM, a tea dance was held at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund, but not all the tourists participated, as some of them felt tired from touring all day.

Magnificent Facilities

The "Lissauer" liner is the second largest liner of the German Hapag-Lloyd Company. It is an all-white gasoline-powered liner, weighing 20,000 tons, 620 feet long, 72 feet wide, and nine stories high. It can travel 42 miles per hour. The facilities inside the ship are extremely perfect, such as swimming pools, billiard rooms, smoking rooms, libraries, dance halls, etc., all fully equipped. When the ship arrived in Shanghai, the pier was temporarily filled with various vendors, creating a lively and bustling scene.

Prince's Conversation

Among the tourists who came yesterday were Prince Rudolph of Hohenzollern-Kinzigburg of Germany, Princess Anna, Prince Adolf of Buschhorn-Liepsbon, and Princess Elizabeth. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited yesterday and first met Princess Elizabeth. The princess spoke fluent English. Later, Elizabeth introduced Prince Adolf and others for a joint interview. They praised China very much, calling China an exotic land. This was their first visit to China, but before coming to Shanghai, they had long heard of China's culture, history, etc., which were not matched by European and Western countries. They regretted that they could not stay in Shanghai and other parts of China for longer on this trip. If there is an opportunity in the future, they plan to come to China again for a longer stay. They then said that they would leave Shanghai tomorrow morning (that is, this morning) and head north to Qinhuangdao, transferring to Peiping (Beijing) for sightseeing. They believed that Peiping, as the ancient capital of China, would surely make them feel even more novel.

Departure for Peiping This Morning

After returning to the ship last night, the tourists were allowed to depart at 8:00 AM this morning, leaving Shanghai and heading north to Qinhuangdao, then transferring to the Beining Railway to visit Peiping. They are scheduled to visit Peiping for three days, then take the original ship from Qinhuangdao to Japan, then through Honolulu and the Panama Canal, and return to the United States, scheduled to return to New York on May 26.

Three Killed, One Injured in Tragic Murder Case on Haichang Road; Sun Jingyu Kills Yang Wenxiang's Wife and Daughters; Bizarre Case of Murder Followed by Suicide 143

At around 7:00 PM the night before last, a thug suddenly appeared at the home of Yang Wenxiang, a barber from Yangzhou, on Haichang Road (near Yaojia Right Bridge) in Zhabei. Yang was not at home at the time. When the thug saw the Yang family, he took out a Mauser pistol and started firing wildly. As a result, Yang's wife, Ji (43 years old), was shot in the chest, with the bullet passing through the front and back. She was shot in the right shoulder, with the bullet passing through the neck and exiting from the left shoulder. Yang Wenxiang's eldest daughter, Yang Kouzi (17 years old), was shot twice in the center of her chest, with the bullets passing through her back. The second daughter, Kou Dizi (15 years old), saw that her mother and sister had been killed and hid under the bed, but she was also shot twice by the thug, once in the left waist and once in the center of her left hand. Seeing that all three had been shot and killed, the thug lay down at the doorway, with his head on the threshold and his feet facing outward, and pointed the Mauser pistol at the center of his forehead and pulled the trigger to commit suicide. The bullet exited from the back of his head. After the incident, neighbors arrived and found that Kou Dizi had not yet died, so they immediately sent her to Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road for treatment. They also rushed to report to the Xinzha Branch Bureau. Director Ruan Kai sent Inspector Jiang Dianle to investigate and confirm the facts. A Mauser pistol and three bullet casings were found next to the thug's body and taken to the bureau. The report was submitted to the Inspection Department of the Public Security Bureau, which ordered the 11th District security guard to report to the Shanghai Local Court to request an autopsy. At around 4:00 PM yesterday, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang, accompanied by Secretary Chen Rong, arrived at the scene. The autopsy confirmed that Yang Ji, Yang Kouzi, and the suicide thug, Sun Jingyu, had died from gunshot wounds sustained while alive. The death certificates were filled out. The bodies of Yang Ji and Yang Kouzi, mother and daughter, were placed in coffins by Yang Wenxiang himself. The body of the thug had not yet been placed in a coffin as of evening.

Zhu Jihuang, Chinese Detective Sergeant of the Hongkou Police, along with Detectives Wang Runhe and Fang Fucheng, learned that someone was secretly selling opium at 710 and 646 Renzhi Lane on North Sichuan Road to make a profit. The accomplices, Xu (from Guangdong), and customers Liang Yongfa, Cen Yuesan, Gu Jimin, and suspect Shi Yiren, were all taken to the police station and detained. Then, Chinese and Western detectives explained the process of solving the case and presented the evidence for inspection. Pitiable Situation of a Woman: Loss of Job Leading to Abortion; Inserts a Strip of Pickled Radish to Induce Abortion; Although the Fetus Was Disturbed, It Was Still Removed by the Hospital — Sentenced to Two Years, Probation Granted 146

Shen Chen, a young woman from Zhenjiang, 39 years old, came to Shanghai due to extreme poverty. Through a recommendation, she was hired as a domestic worker at the home of a Japanese man named Mr. So-and-so at 9 Pingliang Road, Yangshupu. However, she was already pregnant. Fearing that her abdomen would gradually swell, making it inconvenient to work, and causing her employer to dislike her, leading to job loss, she went to the Guangren Hospital on February 6, begging for an abortion. The hospital gently advised against it, stating that abortion without cause is not only unethical but also a cruel act. Although she accepted the advice at the time, she recently had a relapse after privately calculating that she was three months pregnant. She knew that Japanese women were fond of pickled radishes, but they would avoid eating them when pregnant. From this, she deduced that radishes must be harmful to pregnant women. On the evening of the 20th of last month, she asked her employer for leave, claiming that she was going to a wedding feast at a relative's house in Zhabei, and did not return until the next morning. Her employer saw that she looked haggard and asked her about it, but she hesitated and could not answer. Her employer thought she was sick and told her to go to the hospital for treatment. She also felt unbearable pain and went to the Guangren Hospital again for treatment, explaining the cause of her illness. It turned out that on the evening of the 20th, she did not actually go to a banquet but secretly took a strip of pickled radish from her employer's house and inserted it into her vagina in a secluded place, thinking that the fetus would be aborted. However, after one night, although the fetus was disturbed, it did not come out. It formed a state of being neither in nor out. The doctor then performed surgery to remove the fetus and kept her in the hospital for treatment. The hospital reported this to the local police station. Yesterday morning, the police station sent detectives and learned that she had recovered. They took her to the First Special District Local Court. Jiang Baolian, the lawyer representing the police station, filed a public lawsuit against her based on Article 304, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law regarding abortion. He stated the details of the case, presented the hospital's diagnosis certificate, and the strip of pickled radish she used for the abortion as evidence. When questioned, Shen Chen confessed to using a pickled radish to induce an abortion, stating that she came up with the method herself and was not taught by anyone. She did this because she feared losing her job if she was pregnant. After the interrogation, Judge Zhan sentenced her to two years of imprisonment. Considering that the motive for the abortion was purely a matter of livelihood and the circumstances were excusable, he leniently granted her two years of probation.

China's Egg Industry and Hygiene – As Reported by the North-China Daily News' London Correspondent 147

The London correspondent of the North-China Daily News reported on March 29th: I (the correspondent) recently learned about the matter of Chinese liquid eggs being imported into England. Those in China are certainly unaware, which some readers may be interested to hear. This week, someone made unfavorable comments about Chinese eggs. A newspaper even published a report written by a mycologist after examining samples, claiming that they contained excessive mold and could not be considered a satisfactory product. This criticism undoubtedly stems from the pressure of the British Poultry Association. A major importer of Chinese liquid eggs told me in response that China is the main country exporting liquid eggs, something I had never imagined. In 1927, England imported a total of 640,000 CWT (hundredweight, 112 pounds) of liquid eggs, of which 625,500 CWT came from China. Last year, the import figure was 818,370 CWT, with China accounting for 800,765 CWT. However, this actually exceeds the average figure, as British importers, hearing rumors that the government would increase import taxes, made bold and special purchases. Apart from China, Egypt is the next largest exporter of liquid eggs to England, with about 20,000 CWT. The total from other countries is only a few thousand. The merchant who spoke to me said that the vast number of bakeries in England rely on Chinese liquid eggs as their raw material. This industry was unknown thirty years ago and was created by companies such as Lyons and ABC. Therefore, the Chinese liquid egg industry not only provides British shipping companies with approximately £180,000 in freight charges each year, and insurance companies and warehouses with approximately £90,000 in increased income, but also supports the livelihoods of thousands of cooks and bakers, and boosts sales of sugar, flour, raisins, and other industries. If the import of this type of egg product were banned, the enormous losses on all sides would be conceivable. The merchant also showed me photos of Shanghai and Qingdao egg factories at work. The female workers all wear white hats and aprons, presenting a very fresh image. He also mentioned the mycologist's report, saying that the standards mentioned in the report far exceed what England requires. He then asked me, have there been any epidemics caused by eating cakes made with Chinese eggs in England over the years? In fact, there have never been any. Translator's note: China's export industry relies entirely on a few native products. In recent years, silk and tea have plummeted, and other products are also being gradually diminished. Yet, even this small egg product cannot be tolerated and is arbitrarily criticized in the hope of completely eliminating it. Will those of our countrymen who like to use imported goods be moved by reading this account?

Failure to Revive the China-England Dispensary; New Company to be Formed by Depositors; Old Company to be Liquidated and Dissolved 149

China-England Dispensary Co., Ltd. on Nanjing Road, along with its various branches, was previously unable to manage its finances. The shareholders resolved to entrust accountant Xie Lin to declare liquidation. Mr. Xie then convened a meeting of creditors to discuss the matter. It was decided to appoint representatives to explore the possibility of revival. However, the representatives consulted several times, and the depositors' opinions could not be reconciled. The shareholders also had no intention of continuing the business. Yesterday, it was finally decided to liquidate the company according to the law. After the liquidation is completed, the new company will take over, and the old company will be dissolved. The details are as follows:

Creditors' Opinions: The dispensary owes over 161,000 yuan in sales payments and over 179,000 yuan to banks and money shops. Previously, Mr. Xie convened a meeting at the Daya Lou restaurant. The creditors present, seeing that the Jicheng Dispensary had resumed business after closing, mostly advocated that the China-England Dispensary should also find a way to revive. They appointed Meng Xian, Shao Jingfu, and ten others as representatives to carry out the revival based on the results of the creditors' meeting. They consulted several times at Mr. Xie's office and audited the accounts. However, there were many obstacles to the revival, making it difficult to achieve.

Decision to Dissolve: The dispensary owes depositors a massive 783,000 yuan, accounting for more than half of the total claims. If the revival were to proceed, the depositors' opinions would have to be sought. The depositors were concerned that the proposed revival method would involve paying off the deposits over ten years, which they considered too long and uncertain. They did not agree, hindering the progress of the revival. At the same time, the shareholders felt that the domestic economic downturn was worsening and that it would not be easy to turn the business around in the short term. If they decided to revive, they would need to increase capital, but many shareholders were in financial difficulties. They had no confidence in raising funds under the current market conditions and expressed their opposition to the revival.

Formation of a New Company: As a result of the negotiations with the shareholders, it was decided to liquidate the company and entrust Mr. Xie Lin's firm with the liquidation procedures starting on [date missing]. The company will be handed over to a new company, and the original company will be dissolved. Currently, a group of depositors is advocating taking over the dispensary with their deposits and forming a new company. It is said that most depositors have expressed their agreement and are now in the process of organizing the new company. The takeover is expected to happen soon. As for the name, since China-England has a history of over fifty years, the original name of China-England Dispensary will generally be retained, with a distinguishing mark added to differentiate it.

Shanghai Municipal Council Revises Regulations on Freight Trucks 152

The Shanghai Municipal Council, to ensure safety, has adopted the recommendations of the Police and Traffic Committee and revised several points in the existing regulations on freight trucks and trailer licenses. One is to prohibit passengers, whether taking a ride or a chartered trip, from receiving any remuneration. This prohibition does not apply to group passenger vehicles that have separate licenses. In addition, there is often a risk of goods falling from flatbed trucks during transit. It is also inconvenient to install guardrails on the sides of these trucks. It has now been decided that all such flatbed trucks must have wooden strips nailed to both sides to make the edges slightly higher, so that the loaded items are slightly tilted inward to ensure safety. In addition to the driver, only one other person is allowed to ride in the front of the freight truck, and the driver's seat must be partitioned. These regulations are now being prepared for implementation.

Shanghai Municipal Council Restricts Parking in the Central District 153

The Traffic Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council recently stated that although parking of cars on Hankou Road, Jiujiang Road, [missing], Ningbo Road, and other locations in the central district may be permitted by regulations or allowed by custom, the increasing length of new vehicles makes parking and leaving very troublesome, which greatly hinders traffic. It has now been proposed to the Board of Directors to revise Clause 47 of the traffic regulations as follows: 1. On Hankou Road, the section between Jiangxi Road and Henan Road will only allow parallel parking (Ranking) along the roadside on the north side in the future, and will not allow perpendicular parking (Parking). 2. On Jiujiang Road, from the Bund to Henan Road, only parallel parking of cars on the south side will be allowed in the future. 3. On Fuzhou Road, the section between Jiangxi Road and Henan Road will only allow parallel parking of cars on the north side during office hours in the future. 4. On Ningbo Road, the section between Jiangxi Road and Henan Road will only allow parallel parking on the north side in the morning and on the south side in the afternoon in the future. The section between Sichuan Road and Jiangxi Road will be subject to the same regulations as before.

Hu Society Collects Local Products from Huzhou; Displayed and Exhibited at the Society 154

The six counties of Huzhou are the wealthiest areas in western Zhejiang, with abundant products, especially silk and brocade, which are particularly prominent. They have a long history and a considerable reputation in domestic and foreign markets. Since this year, under the pressure of foreign goods and artificial silk, and the influence of the decline of commerce in Inner Mongolia, sales have declined daily. It is now heard that the Huzhou Society in this city, to revitalize local products, plans to use the empty space on the four walls of the society to display samples of local products from the six counties of Huzhou for exhibition, in order to arouse the deep understanding of outsiders and gradually promote them. This measure will be of great benefit to the local products of Huzhou. Ling Jun Songru, the director of the society's affairs department, has prepared measures for collecting and displaying samples of local products and photos of scenic spots and historical sites in Huzhou, which have been discussed and passed by the society's committee and handed over to the society's industrial and affairs departments for implementation. Various forms have now been made and sent to the agencies and organizations in the six counties, requesting them to widely collect the items.

Wang Wenkui Accused of Forcing a Young Woman to Have an Abortion, Resulting in Her Tragic Death; She Was Already Pregnant When They Began Cohabitating, and He Feared Confusion of Lineage, So He Poisoned Her; The Elderly Couple, Distraught Over Their Daughter's Tragic Death, Filed a Private Prosecution 157

Wang Wenkui, also known as Wang Cheng, a native of Ningbo who runs a reed organ factory at No. 12, Tailai Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession, has recently been sued by Ling Songsun (63 years old this year), an elderly man from Suzhou residing on Dajing Road, who has engaged lawyer Gu Jicheng as his agent. The lawsuit was filed with the Criminal Division of the Special District Court, accusing Wang of the crimes of abandonment and injury resulting in death, under Articles 307, Section 2, and 296, Section 2 of the Criminal Code. The plaintiff's statement alleges that the defendant forced an abortion without consent, resulting in serious injury and death, and requests that justice be served and severe punishment be imposed. The plaintiff's family was poor, and their daughter, Xingbao, was introduced to work as a servant in the Wenlan Pavilion brothel on Fuzhou Road at the age of eighteen in 1932. The defendant frequented the establishment and, seeing the beauty of the young woman, seduced her. The young woman, naive and inexperienced, was unable to resist and was lured into the plot. From around June of the same year, Wang repeatedly took her to rooms in the Central Hotel and the Great Shanghai Hotel for cohabitation, despite her parents' dissuasion. Finally, they moved to the front廂房 on the upper floor of No. 3, Lane 2, Handeli, Gulangyu Road, near Nicheng Bridge. On the twentieth day of the seventh lunar month of the same year, the defendant sent someone to inform them that Xingbao was in critical condition after an abortion and asked them to come and see her. When the couple arrived, they found their daughter had died, her eyes staring straight ahead, her lower body covered in bloody filth, and a piece of flesh about two inches long placed on a piece of paper. The couple was heartbroken at the sight and cried out in anguish. The defendant, feeling guilty and fearing exposure, knelt and begged them not to make a scene, promising to support the two elderly for the rest of their lives. After the funeral, the defendant's younger sister, Laoqi (also known as Aunt Qi and Nanny Lingling), also interceded to prevent the matter from escalating. The couple, out of consideration, endured it for a time. Lao Laotai witnessed the scene. Later, the defendant transported the coffin to the Ningbo Guild Hall on Xieqiao, registered it under the name of Wang Cheng, and left it there. When the plaintiff's daughter was cohabiting with the defendant, she was already pregnant. The defendant, fearing that the offspring would confuse the lineage, resorted to this cruel method, treating abortion like child's play and regarding human life as worthless. His viciousness and cruelty surpassed even the most inhumane beasts. The plaintiff's loss of a daughter is a small matter, but humanity is a great matter. If justice is not served, the soul of the deceased will forever be in unrest. Therefore, the lawsuit is filed according to law, requesting that the defendant be arrested and brought to justice, and including a civil suit, requesting that he be ordered to pay damages of 15,000 yuan to punish the lawbreakers and comfort the lonely soul. The court, based on the statement, convened a hearing by Judge Li Changnian the day before yesterday. The defendant did not arrive after being summoned. The plaintiff, represented by a lawyer, stated that they were ill and requested a postponement. The court, after reviewing the report, granted the request and adjourned the hearing to be rescheduled later.

Shanghai-Taiwan Ferry; Collision Between the Maoli and Haiguang Vessels; Accident Occurred in Haimen Port; Maoli Suspended from Service Starting Today 158

The Maoli vessel of the Maoli Shipping Company in this city collided with an Asia Oil Transport vessel in Haimen on its previous trip from Shanghai to Haimen and back to Shanghai yesterday. Both vessels were damaged. The Maoli has been suspended from service for repairs. The details are as follows:

Truth About the Collision

The Maoli vessel of the Maoli Shipping Company sailed from Shanghai to Haimen and Huangyan last Thursday, fully loaded with cargo and passengers. It first arrived at Zhoushan and then sailed to Haimen. At 4:05 AM on March 30th, when it reached the entrance to Haimen Port, the Haiguang, a kerosene tanker of the Asiatic Petroleum Company, was also transporting goods to Haimen for unloading. It had arrived in the port on the 29th and was anchored in the center of the river. The Maoli vessel arrived at Haimen River. Last night, it was during high tide and extremely dark. According to regulations, the fore and aft masthead lights on the Haiguang should have been arranged with the front light higher and the rear light lower. However, on that vessel, the rear light was higher and the front masthead light was lower. As the Maoli vessel was being pushed by the high tide, the captain ordered a turn to dock at the wharf. Unfortunately, during the turn, the Maoli vessel was pushed by the tide and collided with the Haiguang. Both vessels were damaged as a result.

Extent of the Damage

The Haiguang oil tanker was originally anchored in Haimen Port. When the Maoli vessel turned, the collision occurred. According to Captain Xu, the Maoli vessel was fully loaded with cargo and passengers and was heavily affected by the tide. It was impossible to stop the vessel during the turn, resulting in the unfortunate collision. At the time, the Maoli believed that it had collided with the stern of the Haiguang. Unexpectedly, the height of the masthead lights was reversed, and the collision occurred on the left side of the Haiguang's bow. The damage was not very significant. On the Maoli vessel itself, the middle of the right outer hull was dented due to the impact with the Haiguang's bow. The black edge was cut into two sections, but there was no rupture. According to Captain Xu's inspection after the incident, the Haiguang's losses were approximately 300-400 yuan, while the Maoli's hull damage was only around 700-800 yuan.

Repairs in Shanghai

After the accident, the captain of the Maoli vessel and the captain of the Haiguang vessel certified the collision and assessed the damage on the spot. The Maoli then docked to unload cargo and passengers before continuing to Huangyan. It then returned from Haimen to Shanghai. Yesterday, Captain Xu reported the collision to the company and the company forwarded the report to the Maritime Affairs Bureau and sent a letter to the Insurance Association, requesting that personnel be sent to inspect the damage to the vessel. The Maoli Company, to ensure safe navigation, has decided to suspend the Maoli from service starting today and enter the shipyard for repairs. The collision between the Maoli vessel and the Haiguang will result in losses of approximately 3,000 yuan, including the loss of scheduled voyages. The cargo and passengers are all safe.

Amoy Road Drug Syndicate Case Judgement 164

The Yufeng Company at No. 46, Zunde Lane, and the Xinglong Company at No. 48, were a large-scale heroin manufacturing syndicate. The principals, Chen Minghua, Guan Jian, Li Ziqiang, etc., rented a warehouse at No. 236 Guangdong Road. Due to carelessness, a fire broke out involving dangerous goods like ether, resulting in an explosion, collapsing the tail end of the structure and injuring people. After a thorough investigation by Yu A’gen, the Chinese Chief Detective of the relevant Old Zha Gate Police Station, along with detectives He Renrui, Yang Guanying, etc., the following personnel working in the two premises were arrested: Tang Jiejun (also known as Tian Jun, Tian Jiemin), Wang Yonggui, Gao Guoqing, Fan Wenxi, the principal offender Chen Lian, suspects Wu Guoxian, Gou Hechun, and Wen Zong'e, etc. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, prosecuted them separately for offenses under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, etc. After repeated interrogations by the First Special District Court, the case has now concluded. Yesterday morning, Qian Hongye, the presiding judge of the Criminal Court, took the stand in Criminal Court One and announced the verdict: Chen Zonglian is sentenced to three years of imprisonment and fined five thousand yuan for selling opium substitutes. Tang Jiejun, Gao Guoqing, and Fan Wenxi are each sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined two hundred yuan each for assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. Wang Yonggui is sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined two hundred yuan for manufacturing opium substitutes. for aiding in private smuggling is fined three hundred yuan. The number of days of detention before the final judgement will be converted at a rate of two days of detention for one day of imprisonment, or one day of detention for three yuan of fine. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it will be calculated at a rate of three yuan per day, and the imprisonment period shall not exceed one year. The seized heroin, manufacturing equipment, raw materials, drugs, etc., will be confiscated according to the list. Wen Zong'e is found not guilty on the charge of accepting bribes. Wu Guoxian and Gou Hechun are both found not guilty. They remain on bail pending the appeal period.

It is now learned that this case had already concluded one debate, but because the defendant hired lawyers Lin Dawen and Wu Qilun to present a defense during the public hearing, a second debate was held. At 10 o'clock yesterday morning, Liu Enrong, the presiding judge of the Criminal Court, specially opened the Third Court to announce the verdict. He ordered the detained Yan Wanglong to be brought before the court, briefly questioned him about his age and origin, and then rose to announce the verdict: Yan Wanglong is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for perjury. Yan Feng was dissatisfied with the verdict, and the court ordered him to present his reasons and appeal according to law. After the verdict was announced, he was ordered to be returned to custody pending further instructions.

Market Situation Amidst Restrictions on Foreign Rice 172

In order to maintain domestic agricultural production, the government has newly formulated measures to restrict foreign rice, and the Central Bank has raised funds to establish a Food Transportation and Sales Bureau. This has been reported in previous newspapers. According to a conversation with a leader in the rice industry, it is recently rumored that the No. 3 foreign rice, which will be subject to a slightly increased import tax, that is, rice with more than 60 broken grains per hundred grains, is sold for about one yuan cheaper than No. 1 rice because the import tax is reduced by half. Poor people are eager to buy and eat it because of its low price. In fact, the price of the rice merchants ordering from Saigon and other places is no lower than that of No. 1 rice. In total, it is estimated that about 4 million bags of No. 1 and No. 3 foreign rice have been ordered this year, and more than 3 million bags have been shipped one after another, with only about 900,000 bags remaining. Among them, No. 3 rice accounts for less than 100,000 bags. It is expected that it can be sold out in an instant when it is imported. However, since hearing the news of the tax increase, the colleagues have not dared to continue ordering, so the effect of restriction has been achieved invisibly, and the source can be greatly reduced. As for the number already purchased, it is not too much to supply the needs of the people of our country. Moreover, the climate has been extremely cold recently, and the spring harvest has been greatly affected, and the price of rice has tended to rise step by step. If it comes to the time when the old grain is exhausted and the new grain has not yet arrived, it will definitely be even higher, and it is necessary to pre-plan methods of prevention and rescue. Therefore, the existing foreign rice will not hinder domestic agricultural production.
